54→\n    55→type CheckID string\n    56→\n    57→// CheckResult contains the result of checking a pod and indicates whether the pod is allowed,\n    58→// and if not, why it was forbidden.\n    59→//\n    60→// Example output for (false, \"host ports\", \"8080, 9090\"):\n    61→//\n    62→//\tWhen checking all pods in a namespace:\n    63→//\t  disallowed by policy \"baseline\": host ports, privileged containers, non-default capabilities\n    64→//\tWhen checking an individual pod:\n    65→//\t  disallowed by policy \"baseline\": host ports (8080, 9090), privileged containers, non-default capabilities (CAP_NET_RAW)\n    66→type CheckResult struct {\n    67→\t// Allowed indicates if the check allowed the pod.\n    68→\tAllowed bool\n    69→\t// ForbiddenReason must be set if Allowed is false.\n    70→\t// ForbiddenReason should be as succinct as possible and is always output.\n    71→\t// Examples:\n    72→\t// - \"host ports\"\n    73→\t// - \"privileged containers\"\n    74→\t// - \"non-default capabilities\"\n    75→\tForbiddenReason string\n    76→\t// ForbiddenDetail should only be set if Allowed is false, and is optional.\n    77→\t// ForbiddenDetail can include specific values that were disallowed and is used when checking an individual object.\n    78→\t// Examples:\n    79→\t// - list specific invalid host ports: \"8080, 9090\"\n    80→\t// - list specific invalid containers: \"container1, container2\"\n    81→\t// - list specific non-default capabilities: \"CAP_NET_RAW\"\n    82→\tForbiddenDetail string\n    83→}\n    84→\n    85→//
